# JooPark Workspace Product Direction

Updated: 2026-06-10

## Direction Hypothesis

JooPark Workspace should be a local-first personal operating cockpit for one operator: today, tasks, notes, projects, local DB knowledge, and LLM reference material should turn into action without a build step, account, or SaaS backend. It should beat broader references by being smaller, faster to ship, easier to self-host, and more honest about local data boundaries.

## References To Beat

| Reference | Strength to learn from | Gap JooPark can exploit |
| --- | --- | --- |
| AFFiNE | Local-first docs, whiteboards, databases, and AI in one knowledge workspace. Source: https://affine.pro/ | Rich but broad. JooPark can stay narrower and put daily execution first instead of becoming a full canvas suite. |
| AppFlowy | Open-source Notion alternative with docs, notes, wikis, databases, Kanban, calendar, and AI. Source: https://docs.appflowy.io/docs/appflowy/readme/welcome-to-appflowy | Full app ecosystem. JooPark can stay no-build/static and keep data ownership visible in every workflow. |
| Linear | Workspace context becomes action through issues, projects, agents, and automations. Source: https://linear.app/docs/linear-agent | Team SaaS orientation. JooPark can make the same execution bias work for one local operator without workspace setup. |

## Loop 1 Decision

The current app already passes the mobile smoke gate, but the home screen order still overexposes launch/evidence machinery before the actual operating cockpit. Loop 1 therefore keeps all verification surfaces intact but moves the daily execution cards ahead of launch operations, tightens the mobile sidebar, and changes quick-start copy toward task/project/backup execution.

## Loop 2 Decision

The next gap was local data safety. Notion keeps deleted pages recoverable from Trash, Linear points accidental issue deletion first to undo and then archives, and AppFlowy has trash events for put-back and restore-all flows. JooPark is a static localStorage app, so Loop 2 adopts the smallest matching safety layer: immediate deletes for events, todos, notes, habits, issues, tasks, queries, and migrations now show an undo toast that restores the deleted record in place. Larger cascading deletes keep their explicit confirmation modal for now.

## Loop 3 Decision

The undo behavior is now a product contract, not a manual smoke note. Loop 3 adds a dedicated release smoke that opens JooPark in an isolated Chrome profile, deletes and restores all immediate-delete record types, verifies task dependency restoration, and confirms restored records are persisted back into localStorage. The release smoke pipeline now runs this gate before accessibility checks.

## Loop 4 Decision

Undo needs a different timeout from ordinary feedback. Loop 4 keeps normal toasts short but gives undo toasts an eight-second window, then strengthens the delete-undo smoke so it waits longer than the old 3.2-second timeout before restoring the first deleted record.

## Loop 5 Decision

Eight-second undo covers the immediate mistake, but it still fails the safer recovery pattern seen in Notion Trash and Linear Recently deleted archives. Loop 5 adds a bounded local recently-deleted ledger for non-cascading deletes and exposes it in Settings, so a single operator can restore or discard deleted events, todos, notes, habits, issues, tasks, queries, and migrations after the undo toast expires.

## Loop 6 Decision

Recovery should not be hidden behind memory of where Settings lives. Notion makes Trash a navigable workspace surface and Linear exposes recently deleted records through archives, while JooPark already has a compact data-safety sheet in the top bar. Loop 6 keeps the action count stable but changes the existing backup/recovery affordance to show the current recently-deleted count and route the operator to Settings when recovery is available.

## Loop 7 Decision

Trash/recently-deleted patterns are not just about restore; they also need a reliable path to discard records. Loop 7 tightens JooPark's local recovery contract so a discarded or cleared ledger entry cannot be restored by a stale undo toast, then extends the release smoke to prove restore, discard, clear, stale-undo blocking, and persistence in one browser run.

## Loop 8 Decision

Recently-deleted recovery should be bounded by time as well as count. Notion and Linear both communicate 30-day recovery windows, so JooPark now keeps at most 40 local recovery records and prunes records older than 30 days during normalization. The Settings panel exposes the 30-day policy and the delete/undo smoke proves expired records are pruned and persisted.

## Loop 9 Decision

Recovery gets slower once the local ledger contains several record types. Notion Trash supports search and filters, and Linear keeps recently deleted records in an archive surface built for quick restore. Loop 9 adds a Settings-level search box and kind filter for recently-deleted records, including filtered empty states, while keeping the ledger local and non-persistent UI filters out of exported workspace data.

## Loop 10 Decision

The recovery surface should be reachable without remembering the Settings route. Notion exposes Trash as a navigable surface and Linear exposes archives through shortcuts, so JooPark now adds a command-palette entry for recently-deleted recovery. The command routes to Settings, focuses the recovery panel after storage-health rerenders, and the delete/undo smoke proves the command path before restore.

## Loop 11 Decision

Local recovery only earns trust if it survives the same backup boundaries as the rest of the workspace. Notion and AppFlowy both treat recovery/data ownership as part of the user's data lifecycle, so JooPark now verifies that `deletedItems` is accepted as a backup slice, appears in import summaries, and trips its 40-record import limit guard. The release smoke covers this without adding another UI surface.

## Loop 12 Decision

Single-item restore is safe but slow when multiple local records were deleted during the same cleanup pass. AppFlowy-style restore-all behavior fits JooPark's local-first recovery ledger if it remains conservative, so Loop 12 adds a Settings "모두 복구" action that restores every restorable ledger entry, leaves failed duplicates behind, and persists both restored records and ledger cleanup. The delete/undo smoke now proves bulk restore before clear/discard paths.

Loop 12 also tightens the route smoke gate so the root development server is not failed by an optional `release-provenance.json` fallback 404. Packaged release provenance remains covered by the release verifier, while local route smoke now stays focused on app routing, layout, console, and real network regressions.

## Loop 13 Decision

Recovery is now tracked as a release-readiness product contract instead of living only in implementation and browser smoke. Loop 13 adds a `recent_deleted_recovery` audit requirement that checks the local ledger, Settings recovery panel, command-palette route, backup/import persistence boundary, and delete/undo smoke proof. The compact audit summary also exposes this contract under Product Contracts, so operator status checks show whether recently-deleted recovery remains pass even when public-launch blockers are still outstanding.

## Loop 14 Decision

The 30-day recovery window should be actionable at item level, not only implied by the Settings panel header. Loop 14 adds per-row expiry metadata and a visible remaining-days badge for recently-deleted records, then extends the delete/undo smoke and release audit contract so every recovery row must expose its expiry timestamp, bounded remaining days, and visible expiry label.

Loop 14 also applies the existing root-dev `release-provenance.json` 404 exception to mobile smoke, not just desktop route smoke. The packaged release still verifies provenance as a release artifact, while local mobile smoke remains focused on responsive layout and interaction regressions.

## Loop 15 Decision

The next product gap is calendar execution, not more launch machinery. Direction check: JooPark already behaves like a local-first cockpit for data safety, but the Calendar surface still forced a single month grid and made daily execution slower than the references. A/B research: AppFlowy's official Calendar View supports switching between month, week, and day views, while Linear's official Display Options and Custom Views docs emphasize quickly changing how work is displayed and saving useful perspectives. JooPark adopts the useful part without adding SaaS/team-view weight: the Calendar now has 월/주/일 segmented controls, range-aware prev/next navigation, selected-day agenda continuity, mobile-safe week/day layouts, and `m`/`w`/`d` shortcuts for one-operator time-scale switching.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 15 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| AppFlowy Calendar View | Month/week/day calendar switching for date-backed work. Source: https://appflowy-io-appflowy.mintlify.app/core/calendar-view | Broad database workspace with heavier app surface. | Add local 월/주/일 calendar modes inside the static runtime. |
| Linear Display Options / Custom Views | Fast view changes and reusable work perspectives. Sources: https://linear.app/docs/display-options and https://linear.app/docs/custom-views | Team SaaS and saved workspace views are more than a solo local cockpit needs. | Add immediate time-scale controls and keyboard shortcuts without accounts or backend state. |

Loop 15 changed `calendar-view.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `package.json`. Verification: `node --check` for edited JS files, `npm run lint`, `npm run check:structure`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed; `npm run verify` still fails only on remote workflow installation/readiness gates that require GitHub workflow-scope setup, while packaged browser gates pass. Next loop should continue product-first improvements by making the remaining PM execution surface more direct, with Kanban drag/drop/order persistence or DB catalog truthfulness as the likely next candidate.

## Loop 16 Decision

The next product gap is Kanban execution order, not another launch-proof panel. Direction check: the board already moved issues between status lanes, but a solo operator still could not express "this card first" inside a lane or trust that order after rerender/export. A/B research: AppFlowy's Kanban architecture treats cards as database records whose grouping changes through drag/drop, and its shortcuts support fast card operations; Linear's Board layout docs explicitly call out moving a selected issue to the top or bottom of a column and preserving mouse placement when dropped. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: every issue now has a lane-local `order`, board rendering sorts by it, drag/drop can place before or after a target card, and compact top/bottom controls plus `Alt/Option+Shift+Up/Down` persist order without adding a team SaaS workflow.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 16 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| AppFlowy Kanban Board | Cards are database records grouped into board states, and drag/drop changes the grouping cell. Source: https://docs.appflowy.io/docs/documentation/software-contributions/architecture/frontend/database-view/kanban-board | AppFlowy's full database/group management model is heavier than JooPark's current PM slice. | Keep status grouping but add a simple persisted `order` field per issue. |
| Linear Board layout | Board layout supports fast top/bottom moves and mouse placement inside columns. Source: https://linear.app/docs/board-layout | Linear's team workspace, view options, and saved view model are more than the local cockpit needs. | Add compact reorder controls, keyboard top/bottom moves, and drop placement in the static local runtime. |

Loop 16 changed `kanban-view.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check kanban-view.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `npm run lint`, `npm run check:structure`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The release-readiness summary still fails only on the known remote workflow installation/API installer blockers, with external claim guarded until GitHub workflow-scope setup and post-publish proof are complete. Next loop should keep improving product-first daily operation, with DB catalog truthfulness or Kanban lane-level density/selection as the likely next candidate.

## Loop 17 Decision

The next product gap is DB catalog truthfulness. Direction check: JooPark's DB Catalog was already labeled as a local reference, but individual CPU, query, migration, and backup values still looked like current live telemetry. A/B research: OpenMetadata's data asset views separate asset context, profiler, and quality evidence, while DataHub frames freshness as a trust signal for whether data can be relied on. JooPark adopts the useful part without pretending to have connectors: every DB catalog record now carries a `catalogSource` and `catalogUpdatedAt`, the DB surface shows a local/no-live-connection boundary, sample data is visibly stale, and manual edits are stamped fresh so the operator can tell which facts are local notes versus shipped examples.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 17 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| OpenMetadata Data Asset Tabs | Asset pages separate schema/profile/quality context so users can judge trust from adjacent evidence. Source: https://docs.open-metadata.org/latest/how-to-guides/guide-for-data-users/data-asset-tabs | OpenMetadata assumes a connected metadata platform and ingestion pipeline. | Add record-level provenance badges while keeping the catalog static and local. |
| DataHub Data Freshness | Freshness is treated as an explicit trust boundary for operational decisions. Source: https://datahub.com/learn/data-freshness/ | DataHub's observability model is built for live data platform integration. | Mark shipped sample records stale and stamp manual local edits as fresh. |

Loop 17 changed `db-catalog.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check db-catalog.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction and release smoke now prove DB catalog provenance through `dbCatalogProvenance: true`. Next loop should continue product-first operation, likely by making stale DB catalog records more actionable or by tightening Kanban density/selection.

## Loop 18 Decision

The next product gap is making DB catalog provenance actionable. Direction check: Loop 17 made each DB record honest about source and freshness, but the operator still had to scan every instance, table, query, backup, and migration to find stale sample facts. A/B research: OpenMetadata's discovery guide emphasizes keyword search plus quick filters for narrowing assets by owner, tag, service, database, schema, columns, last updated, and related facets; DataHub's freshness material treats freshness issues as health signals that should be surfaced through search filters and asset indicators. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: the DB catalog now has an all/stale sample/manual/imported provenance filter shared across DB tabs, with counts, pressed states, filter empty states, and no live-connector claims.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 18 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| OpenMetadata Discovery | Search and quick filters narrow data assets by relevant metadata facets. Source: https://docs.open-metadata.org/v1.11.x/how-to-guides/data-discovery/discover | OpenMetadata depends on indexed metadata, owners, services, and ingestion-backed asset graphs. | Add lightweight local provenance filters without introducing a metadata backend. |
| DataHub Freshness Monitoring | Freshness is a data health signal, and health/freshness issues can be surfaced through search filters. Source: https://datahub.com/learn/data-freshness/ | DataHub's freshness assertions require live warehouse signals and observability setup. | Add a static `stale sample` queue and keep manual/imported records separable. |

Loop 18 changed `db-catalog.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check db-catalog.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, and `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs` all passed. The interaction smoke now proves the new filter contract through `dbCatalogProvenanceFilter: true`. Next loop should move to a different operator bottleneck, with Kanban density/selection or LLM wiki actionability as the strongest candidates.

## Loop 19 Decision

The next product gap is Kanban scan density. Direction check: Loop 16 made lane order trustworthy, but the board still used the same full card shape even when the operator only needed to scan IDs, titles, assignees, due dates, and progress. A/B research: Linear's Display Options let issue views choose which information appears on board/list items, and its Board Layout docs explicitly note that board cards have limited space and not every property can fit; AppFlowy's feature overview calls out Compact Mode for increasing information density in grid and Kanban views. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: Kanban now has a persisted 표준/압축 density toggle under the existing filter bar. 압축 mode hides label rows and long checklist text while keeping priority, title, assignee, due date, execution count, and progress meter visible.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 19 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Linear Display Options / Board Layout | Views can choose displayed issue properties, and cards deliberately omit details when space is constrained. Sources: https://linear.app/docs/display-options and https://linear.app/docs/board-layout | Linear's full view-options system is larger than a solo local cockpit needs. | Add one persisted density preference instead of a full property-visibility editor. |
| AppFlowy Compact Mode | Compact mode increases information density in grid and Kanban views. Source: https://appflowy-io-appflowy.mintlify.app/features | AppFlowy's database view system carries independent filters, sorts, and field visibility across database views. | Add a lightweight compact Kanban mode inside the existing static board. |

Loop 19 changed `kanban-view.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check kanban-view.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction smoke now proves the density contract through `kanbanDensityPersistence: true`. Next loop should likely move to LLM wiki actionability or a command-palette bridge from knowledge to execution.

## Loop 20 Decision

The next product gap is LLM wiki actionability. Direction check: the wiki already has source-rich articles, but the operator had to manually copy ideas into tasks, notes, or project issues before anything became work. A/B research: Linear issue creation supports fast issue drafting and prefilled issue fields, Linear issue documents keep specs attached to work, AppFlowy combines docs, notes, wikis, databases, Kanban, and AI, and AFFiNE frames documents, whiteboards, and databases as one connected workspace. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: each wiki article now exposes an execution bar that creates a sourced todo, pinned note, or Kanban issue, and the command palette shows the same wiki-to-issue/note/todo actions while a wiki article is open.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 20 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Linear issue creation and issue documents | Issue creation is a primary action, supports prefilled fields, and documents attach specs/resources to work. Sources: https://linear.app/docs/creating-issues and https://linear.app/docs/issue-documents | Linear assumes teams, workspaces, sync, and SaaS issue/document storage. | Create local todo/note/issue drafts from the active wiki article with source metadata. |
| AppFlowy docs/wiki/database surface | AppFlowy combines docs, notes, wikis, databases, Kanban, calendar, and AI in one product. Source: https://docs.appflowy.io/docs/appflowy/readme/welcome-to-appflowy | AppFlowy's full editor/database ecosystem is heavier than the current no-build cockpit. | Keep the wiki static but add direct local execution actions. |
| AFFiNE page docs | AFFiNE positions documents as connected to structured data and planning surfaces. Source: https://affine.pro/pagedoc | AFFiNE's whiteboard/collaboration model is larger than a solo static workspace needs. | Bridge knowledge to local action without adding collaborative document infrastructure. |

Loop 20 changed `llm-wiki-view.js`, `command-palette.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check llm-wiki-view.js`, `node --check command-palette.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-llm-wiki.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction smoke now proves `llmWikiActionDrafts: true` and `llmWikiPaletteBridge: true`.

## Loop 21 Decision

The next product gap is wiki execution feedback. Direction check: Loop 20 could create local drafts, but returning to the article still looked identical, so the operator had to remember whether the article had already produced a todo, note, or issue. A/B research: Linear issue documents keep resources attached to the work item, and Linear's local issue drafts make creation state explicit; AppFlowy and AFFiNE both sell the value of connected knowledge surfaces rather than disconnected notes. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: article cards now show an `실행 n/3` badge when wiki-derived drafts exist, and the article execution bar marks each generated todo/note/issue button as `생성됨` while keeping the click behavior as "open the existing target" instead of creating duplicates.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 21 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Linear issue documents and drafts | Work and supporting documents stay visibly connected, and issue drafting has explicit state. Sources: https://linear.app/docs/issue-documents and https://linear.app/docs/creating-issues | Linear depends on synced issue/document infrastructure. | Show local wiki-to-action state through badges and generated-button states. |
| AppFlowy / AFFiNE connected workspaces | Knowledge, docs, databases, and task surfaces are framed as connected spaces. Sources: https://docs.appflowy.io/docs/appflowy/readme/welcome-to-appflowy and https://affine.pro/pagedoc | Full block-editor/database/whiteboard systems are larger than JooPark needs. | Surface lightweight local connections with sourceKey-derived action state. |

Loop 21 changed `llm-wiki-view.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check llm-wiki-view.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-llm-wiki.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction smoke now proves `llmWikiActionState: true`.

## Loop 22 Decision

The next product gap is wiki execution filtering. Direction check: Loop 21 made wiki-derived action state visible, but the operator still had to scan every article to find which ideas had already been turned into local work and which remained untouched. The same references still apply: Linear keeps work creation and supporting resources visibly connected, while AppFlowy and AFFiNE emphasize connected knowledge and work surfaces. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: the LLM wiki now has `전체 / 미실행 / 실행됨` filters, scoped to the active category or search, so actioned articles become an explicit queue without introducing accounts, sync, or a full saved-view system.

Loop 22 changed `llm-wiki-view.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check llm-wiki-view.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `git diff --check`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-llm-wiki.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction and packaged release smoke now prove `llmWikiActionFilter: true`.

## Loop 23 Decision

The next product gap is DB catalog actionability. Direction check: Loop 17 and Loop 18 made the catalog honest and filterable, but stale sample records still stopped at passive visibility. A/B research remains the same: OpenMetadata separates asset context from profiler/quality evidence, while DataHub treats freshness as a trust signal that should drive action. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: the DB catalog provenance panel now exposes a stale sample review action that creates a sourced Kanban issue with counts, sample records, a no-live-connection boundary, and a checklist for converting stale sample facts into manual local records.

Loop 23 changed `db-catalog.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check db-catalog.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `git diff --check`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction and packaged release smoke now prove `dbCatalogStaleAction: true`.

## Loop 24 Decision

The next product gap is Kanban source visibility. Direction check: JooPark can now create issues from wiki articles, benchmark reviews, and DB catalog stale-sample review, but the Kanban board still rendered those action-derived issues as ordinary cards. The connected-workspace references still matter here: Linear issue documents keep supporting context attached to work, while AppFlowy/AFFiNE emphasize connected knowledge and execution surfaces. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: Kanban cards now show compact source badges for `LLM Wiki`, `DB Catalog`, and review-derived issues, and issue creation flows set the active project so the newly created sourced issue is visible immediately.

Loop 24 changed `kanban-view.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check kanban-view.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `git diff --check`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction and packaged release smoke now prove `kanbanSourceBadges: true`.

## Loop 25 Decision

The next product gap is Kanban source filtering. Direction check: Loop 24 made action-derived issues visible with source badges, but the operator still had to visually scan mixed lanes to isolate wiki, DB catalog, or review-originated work. The connected-workspace references still apply: Linear keeps work and supporting context attached, while AppFlowy/AFFiNE frame knowledge and execution as connected surfaces. JooPark adopts the useful part locally: the Kanban board now has an `전체 / LLM Wiki / DB Catalog / Review / Source` source filter with counts, pressed states, source-aware search, and empty states, without adding a saved-view system or remote workspace assumptions.

Loop 25 changed `kanban-view.js`, `app.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check kanban-view.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `git diff --check`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction and packaged release smoke now prove `kanbanSourceFilter: true`. The release-readiness summary still fails only on the known remote workflow installation/API installer blockers, with packaged browser gates still reported as `not_run` by the audit summary despite `npm test` passing the packaged browser gates.

## Loop 26 Decision

The next product gap is Kanban source-filter recovery. Direction check: Loop 25 could isolate sourced issues, but a zero-result source filter still collapsed into four quiet empty lanes, leaving the operator without an obvious next action. JooPark adopts the same local, no-saved-view approach: when a selected source has no cards under the current project/search/priority constraints, the board now shows a single source-specific empty panel with the active source label and a direct `전체 출처 보기` recovery action.

Loop 26 changed `kanban-view.js`, `styles.css`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check kanban-view.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `git diff --check`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction and packaged release smoke now prove `kanbanSourceEmpty: true`. The release-readiness summary still fails only on the known remote workflow installation/API installer blockers, with packaged browser gates still reported as `not_run` by the audit summary despite `npm test` passing the packaged browser gates.

## Loop 27 Decision

The next product gap is keyboard access to sourced work queues. Direction check: Kanban now has source badges, source filters, and clearable empty states, but the operator still has to navigate to Kanban and visually find the filter group before isolating wiki, DB catalog, review, or generic sourced issues. JooPark adopts the command-palette part of the connected-workspace pattern: the palette now exposes `Kanban: ... 출처 보기` actions for all source filters, so source-backed work queues can be opened from the keyboard without adding saved views or extra navigation chrome.

Loop 27 changed `command-palette.js`, `app.js`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check command-palette.js`, `node --check app.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `git diff --check`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-mobile.mjs`, `node scripts/smoke-a11y.mjs`, and `npm test` all passed. The interaction and packaged release smoke now prove `kanbanSourcePalette: true`. The release-readiness summary still fails only on the known remote workflow installation/API installer blockers, with packaged browser gates still reported as `not_run` by the audit summary despite `npm test` passing the packaged browser gates.

## Loop 28 Decision

The next product gap is release-gate observability. Direction check: Loop 25 through Loop 27 all passed `npm test`, but the quick release-readiness summary still reported packaged browser gates as `not_run` because the successful `smoke-release` run did not refresh the audit cache. That made the operator status surface contradict the real packaged browser proof. JooPark now writes `autoresearch-results/release-readiness-gates.json` directly from a successful `scripts/smoke-release.mjs` run, using the same source commit and source-file SHA-256 fingerprint that the audit summary validates, so `npm test` and `node scripts/audit-release-readiness.mjs --format=summary` agree without rerunning browser gates.

Verification: `node --check scripts/smoke-release.mjs`, `git diff --check`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, and `npm test` all passed. ## Loop 101 Decision

The next product gap is operator-visible release gate evidence depth. External reference check: Linear project status gives stakeholders a quick lifecycle/progress signal, Linear project updates combine a health indicator with richer status/challenges/next-step context, GitHub Actions surfaces workflow run result/logs/artifacts for diagnosis, and Notion's status property reduces ambiguity by grouping work into standard progress categories. JooPark already had deep packaged gate cache validation, but the System Status release gate item only said the broad smoke suite passed; it did not show the concrete evidence an operator needs to compare current state, proof depth, and remaining blockers in one place. ## Loop 125 Decision

The next product gap is making the accessible receipt detail resilient beyond hover/title behavior. Direction check: Loop 124 added `title` and `aria-label` so hidden score and driver details were recoverable, but `title` remains advisory and is not a reliable long-description channel for every input mode. External reference check: MDN documents `aria-description`/`aria-describedby` as ways to provide longer contextual information, MDN's `title` attribute page calls out accessibility concerns, and MDN's accessible-description glossary describes `aria-describedby` as explicit description text in the accessibility tree. A/B comparison: Option A keeps the hidden receipt detail in title/label only; Option B keeps the compact visible receipt, keeps the title as a hover hint, and adds a keyboard-focusable note connected to hidden DOM text with `aria-describedby`. JooPark now adopts Option B so the mixed Todo/PM cockpit remains visually dense while its full ranking receipt is available through real DOM description text. References: https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/Accessibility/ARIA/Reference/Attributes/aria-description, https://developer.mozilla.org/docs/Web/HTML/Reference/Global_attributes/title, https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Glossary/Accessible_description.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 125 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| MDN `aria-description` / `aria-describedby` | Descriptions can provide longer context beyond a concise label. | A raw label alone can collapse detailed ranking evidence into a name. | Use `aria-describedby` to connect the receipt to hidden detailed text. |
| MDN `title` attribute | Title can provide advisory hover information. | Title has accessibility concerns and should not be the only detail path. | Keep title as a hint, not the sole receipt detail channel. |
| MDN accessible description | Explicitly referenced description text enters the accessibility tree. | Machine-readable `data-*` alone does not help assistive-technology users. | Add a `.sr-only` receipt description and smoke gate it. |

Loop 125 changed `app.js`, `scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `scripts/audit-release-readiness.mjs`, and this direction log. Verification: `node --check app.js`, `node --check scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs`, `node --check scripts/audit-release-readiness.mjs`, `npm run check:structure`, `npm run lint`, `git diff --check -- app.js scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs scripts/audit-release-readiness.mjs styles.css docs/product-direction.md`, `node scripts/smoke-interactions.mjs` with `homeExecutionQueueReceiptDescription=true`, `npm test` with `homeExecutionQueueReceiptDescription=true` and `cache.written=true`, and `node scripts/audit-release-readiness.mjs --format=summary` (`274 pass, 0 fail, 0 not_run, 0 blocked`) passed. ## Loop 126 Decision

The next product gap is protecting the home execution queue from becoming the next source of monolithic `app.js` growth. Direction check: Loops 116-125 made the mixed Todo/PM receipt increasingly explainable, but the renderer stayed inline and pushed `app.js` close to the `maxAppLines` structure guard. External reference check: MDN's JavaScript modules guide frames modules as the mechanism complex projects use to split JavaScript into separate pieces, and web.dev's JavaScript performance guidance recommends splitting JavaScript into smaller chunks so the startup path stays responsive. A/B comparison: Option A keeps the home execution queue renderer inline and spends more `app.js` budget on future receipt edits; Option B extracts the renderer into a static runtime helper while keeping ranking models, state transitions, and delegated actions in `app.js`. JooPark now adopts Option B with a conservative no-build helper loaded before `app.js`, rather than switching the whole app to browser ES modules in one jump. References: https://developer.mozilla.org/en-US/docs/Web/JavaScript/Guide/Modules, https://web.dev/learn/performance/code-split-javascript, https://web.dev/articles/reduce-javascript-payloads-with-code-splitting.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 126 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| MDN JavaScript modules | Splitting complex JavaScript into modules improves code organization and browser-native loading is broadly supported. | A full ES module migration would change the app's current classic-script release contract. | Extract the execution queue renderer behind `JooParkHomeExecutionView` and keep script order explicit. |
| web.dev code-split JavaScript | Smaller chunks reduce startup parsing/execution pressure and make future performance work easier to reason about. | The queue is still needed on the home route, so this is a maintainability split rather than lazy loading. | Move dense queue HTML into `home-execution-view.js` without hiding the existing first-screen cockpit. |
| web.dev payload reduction | Route/component-level splitting is simpler than treating a whole app as one bundle. | JooPark is a no-build static SPA, so bundler-driven chunks would add unnecessary release complexity now. | Keep packaging/offline/no-cache gates for the new helper instead of introducing a bundler. |

## Loop 127 Decision

The next product gap is making the packaged browser gate summary cache self-diagnostic. Direction check: Loop 126 proved the full verification ladder, but the first `verify:full` pass exposed a bootstrap fragility where `autoresearch-results/release-readiness-summary.json` could package a stale or incomplete cache shape and leave System Status with less diagnostic detail than the CLI audit. External reference check: GitHub Actions treats dependency cache state, workflow artifacts, and workflow run logs as separate evidence surfaces, so JooPark's packaged summary should carry the cache status plus the mismatch detail an operator needs without opening a terminal. A/B comparison: Option A keeps the compact summary cache with only high-level packaged gate fields and relies on terminal audit diagnostics for `context_mismatch` or incomplete evidence; Option B stores `cache.status`, `issues`, `contextMismatches`, `cachedEvidenceStatus`, and `cachedResultStatus` inside `release-readiness-summary.json`. JooPark now adopts Option B so the packaged System Status panel and quick audit summary share the same diagnostic cache truth. References: https://docs.github.com/en/actions/reference/workflows-and-actions/dependency-caching, https://docs.github.com/en/actions/how-tos/manage-workflow-runs/download-workflow-artifacts, https://docs.github.com/en/actions/how-tos/monitor-workflows/use-workflow-run-logs.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 127 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| GitHub Actions dependency caching | Cache hits and misses are explicit state, and cache contents cannot be mutated after creation. | JooPark does not hide cache reuse behind a single cached boolean. | Persist summary-level cache diagnostics with `status`, freshness, and cached evidence/result status. |
| GitHub workflow artifacts | Workflow outputs can be downloaded and inspected separately from the workflow run page. | The packaged release should not require live GitHub access to inspect local gate evidence. | Package `release-readiness-summary.json` with enough cache detail for System Status and smoke checks. |
| GitHub workflow run logs | Run logs keep diagnostic messages near each job's execution result. | Operators should not need terminal-only logs to understand why cached packaged gates are rejected. | Carry `issues` and `contextMismatches` into the packaged summary cache. |

Loop 127 changed `scripts/audit-release-readiness.mjs`, `README.md`, `autoresearch-results/release-readiness-summary.json`, and this direction log. ## Loop 150 Decision

Direction check: Loop 168 fixed selected file-level ledger commands, but `data/remote-workflow-file-check.json.workflowScopeApprovalHandoff.fallback` still said to use "GitHub UI new-file links to create both workflow files" even when the current live remediation is `replace_existing_remote_file` for an existing Pages workflow with a SHA mismatch and Drift Watch is already verified. External reference check: GitHub documents editing existing repository files through the web file editor, the repository contents API requires the blob SHA when updating an existing file, and manual workflow dispatch requires the workflow file to be configured on the default branch before a run can be triggered. A/B comparison: Option A keeps the generic new-file fallback and relies on the per-row edit URL to correct it later; Option B makes the fallback text itself choose by `installAction`, saying to use edit-file pages for existing mismatched files, new-file pages only for missing files, and no edit for already verified files. JooPark adopts Option B so the install packet's high-level fallback no longer contradicts the current repair action.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 169 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| GitHub repository file editor | GitHub documents direct editing of existing repository files. Source: https://docs.github.com/en/repositories/working-with-files/managing-files/editing-files | A fallback headline should not imply file creation when the workflow already exists. | Generate fallback text from create/edit/ready workflow counts. |
| GitHub Contents API create/update endpoint | Updating an existing file requires existing-file context such as the blob SHA. Source: https://docs.github.com/en/rest/repos/contents#create-or-update-file-contents | The packet should preserve replacement context for `replace_existing_remote_file`. | Require fallback text to mention `installAction` and reject new-file guidance for replacement rows. |
| GitHub manual workflow dispatch | Manual dispatch requires a `workflow_dispatch` workflow on the default branch. Source: https://docs.github.com/en/actions/how-tos/manage-workflow-runs/manually-run-a-workflow | Better fallback wording must not authorize dispatch. | Keep `remoteWorkflowFilesReady=false`, `allDispatchReady=false`, and external claim guards blocked. |

## Loop 170 Decision

The next product gap is testable repo-option parsing for candidate snapshot maintenance. Direction check: recent bug loops hardened release scripts against missing option values, but `check-candidate-freshness-drift.mjs` and `refresh-candidate-snapshot.mjs` still had their `--repo` collector only implicitly covered by smoke commands; a future refactor could again treat `--repo --live` or `--repo --write` as a repository value and skew GitHub-related candidate maintenance. External reference check: Node.js exposes CLI arguments as the trailing entries of `process.argv`, strict Node assertions treat `assert.deepEqual` like `deepStrictEqual` in strict mode, and GitHub CLI repo inventory remains owner-scoped, so repo filters must be explicit and reproducible. A/B comparison: Option A keeps the collector as an untestable closure over `rawArgs`; Option B preserves runtime behavior while allowing tests to inject an args array and lock `--repo=value`, `--repo value`, and missing-value cases. JooPark adopts Option B so candidate freshness and snapshot refresh helpers keep predictable repo filtering before any live GitHub refresh.

| Reference | Strength | Limitation JooPark avoids | Loop 170 adoption |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Node.js `process.argv` | The official API defines additional command-line arguments as the remaining array entries after the Node binary and script path. Source: https://nodejs.org/docs/latest/api/process.html#processargv | Raw positional arrays make missing option values easy to misread as the next flag. | Keep explicit flag-value parsing and test the missing-value edge cases. |
| Node.js assert strict mode | In strict assertion mode, `assert.deepEqual()` behaves like `assert.deepStrictEqual()`. Source: https://nodejs.org/api/assert.html | VM-extracted helper arrays can fail strict realm-sensitive comparisons even when values match. | Spread helper results into the test context before comparing arrays. |
| GitHub CLI `gh repo list` | The official manual states repo listing is scoped to the provided owner and does not traverse ownership boundaries. Source: https://cli.github.com/manual/gh_repo_list | Candidate maintenance should not accidentally broaden or empty repo scope because a flag was consumed as a repo name. | Lock repo option guards for both snapshot drift and refresh helpers. |

Loop 170 changes `scripts/check-candidate-freshness-drift.mjs`, `scripts/refresh-candidate-snapshot.mjs`, `scripts/test-pure-helpers.mjs`, and this direction log. Direction check: `dialog-shell.js` owns notification trigger expansion when opening and closing sheets, but `app.js` still kept an unused `setNotificationTriggerExpanded` wrapper. Structure and release audits already verify the module-owned expansion behavior, so keeping the app wrapper only preserves a compatibility alias with no product caller. A/B comparison: Option A keeps the wrapper as a harmless alias; Option B removes the unused app wrapper while continuing to verify `dialogShellCall` sheet/modal delegation and module-owned `setNotificationTriggerExpanded`. JooPark adopts Option B so dialog shell accessibility ownership stays in the runtime module and the app surface keeps shrinking.

Loop 199 changes `app.js`, `scripts/test-pure-helpers.mjs`, and this direction log. Baseline dialogShellUnusedWrapperCount was `1`: `setNotificationTriggerExpanded` existed in `app.js` with no app-level callers. Candidate count is `0`, with pure helper coverage proving the app wrapper stays removed while `dialogShellCall("openSheet")`, `dialogShellCall("closeSheet")`, `dialogShellCall("openModal")`, `dialogShellCall("trapTab")`, and module-owned `setNotificationTriggerExpanded` remain present. Verification will run syntax checks, focused unit coverage, unit, lint, docs, structure, release-readiness summary, verify:full, and `git diff --check`. External completion remains withheld because GitHub main still has a Pages workflow mismatch, so `remoteWorkflowFilesReady=false`, `allDispatchReady=false`, `launchPacketReadyForExternalClaim=false`, and `readyForExternalClaim=false`.

## Loop 207 Decision

The next product gap is breaking a self-reinforcing full-verify evidence sync loop after product direction changes. Direction check: `npm run verify:full` starts with release-readiness gates and previously stopped on the first failing or blocked step. When release-readiness failed only because `autoresearch-results/verify-workspace-summary.json` still pointed at the previous product-loop experiment, the runner never reached `product_loop_summary_sync`, so the stale experiment stayed stale and the next audit failed for the same reason. A/B comparison: Option A keeps early exit for every failure and requires manual sync plus manual summary repair; Option B keeps early exit for default `npm run verify`, but in `--sync-artifacts` mode continues through launch-readiness and product-loop sync while preserving the overall verify status as fail if any step failed. JooPark adopts Option B so full verify can refresh its own evidence trail without hiding release gate failures.

Loop 207 changes `scripts/verify-workspace.mjs`, `scripts/test-pure-helpers.mjs`, `scripts/audit-release-readiness.mjs`, and this direction log. Baseline fullVerifyArtifactSyncAfterGateFailureCoverage was `0/1`: a release gate fail stopped the sync steps before product-loop parity could catch up. Candidate coverage is `1/1` with source guards proving `if (result.status !== "pass" && !syncArtifacts) break;`, so default verify still exits early while `verify:full` reaches the artifact sync steps and keeps the final status tied to failed steps plus evidenceSync. Verification will run syntax checks, focused unit coverage, unit, lint, docs, structure, release-readiness summary, verify:full, and `git diff --check`. External completion remains withheld because the branch is still ahead of its tracking branch and GitHub main still requires workflow parity, so `publish_branch_sync=blocked`, `remoteWorkflowFilesReady=false`, `allDispatchReady=false`, `launchPacketReadyForExternalClaim=false`, and `readyForExternalClaim=false`.
